<span id="freeTextContainer8637768512530367785">"A triumph."<br /><br />HARPERS<br /><br />Ben Joe Hawkes is a worrier. Raised by his mother, grandmother, and a flock of busy sisters, he's always felt the outsider. When he learns that one of his sisters has left her husband, he heads for home and back into the confusion of childhood memories and unforseen love....</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer111507807">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13529960532714942709">Oh my goodness...one of the most pointless books I've ever read, with an irritatingly disconnected main character who doesn't seem to understand anyone or anything in life, including himself. I never understood why he did or said anything, and he always seems to be in some sort of stupor that makes you feel like you're in a cloud yourself reading it, just grasping for something that makes sense! I couldn't relate to a thing in it and I'm not even sure why I finished it! Now that I know it was he</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13529960532714942709">Oh my goodness...one of the most pointless books I've ever read, with an irritatingly disconnected main character who doesn't seem to understand anyone or anything in life, including himself. I never understood why he did or said anything, and he always seems to be in some sort of stupor that makes you feel like you're in a cloud yourself reading it, just grasping for something that makes sense! I couldn't relate to a thing in it and I'm not even sure why I finished it! Now that I know it was her first novel, I'm a bit more understanding. But still. Just a weird book.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/28357676-fay-roberts" class="left imgcol" title="Fay Roberts"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448535938p2/28357676.jpg" alt="Fay Roberts" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1308310634?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/28357676-fay-roberts" class="user" title="Fay Roberts">Fay Roberts</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/865765.If_Morning_Ever_Comes" title="Paperback 9780099539100" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1308310634">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1818781480365751729">A beautiful stack of Anne Tyler novels have been staring reproachfully down at me from my living room shelf since I received them as a gift. I thought I might as well start from the beginning and quickly looked her up on Wikipedia to get a list. <br /><br />I was surprised to find that Tyler had "disowned" her first two novels but I'm always game to try so shrugged it off and added it to my Goodreads shelf where a long list of two starred reviews popped up beneath it. I quickly skimmed some and decided to j</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1818781480365751729">A beautiful stack of Anne Tyler novels have been staring reproachfully down at me from my living room shelf since I received them as a gift. I thought I might as well start from the beginning and quickly looked her up on Wikipedia to get a list. <br /><br />I was surprised to find that Tyler had "disowned" her first two novels but I'm always game to try so shrugged it off and added it to my Goodreads shelf where a long list of two starred reviews popped up beneath it. I quickly skimmed some and decided to just get on with it and I'm so glad I did.<br /><br />I was entranced with the slow meandering style which mimics the Southern Ben Joe's attitude. I loved the way important information was drip fed to us to build up a picture of the Hawke's family life. They are strange and quirky and I bet they seemed even more so to the reader when first published in the 1960's. <br /><br />The novel was timeless. People are always people so despite the fact that no one had an i-pad or spent their time texting the novel could have been set today. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this portrait of family life and the feeling of disconnection and discontent a lot of people experience of leaving home for the first time. The book has been touted in a lot of reviews as "pointless" but for me that was the point. Life is pointless, there is no beginning, middle and end, this was a snapshot of a few days in Ben Joe's life not his whole life. There was no major catalyst leading to dramatic scenes despite the fact that some life changing and dramatic things were happening. <br /><br />It reminded me a lot of Meave Binchy novels.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1818781480365751729">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_237437527">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237437527" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4969273-kay" class="left imgcol" title="Kay"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Kay" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/237437527?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4969273-kay" class="user" title="Kay">Kay</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/112321.If_Morning_Ever_Comes" title="Paperback 9780449911785" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4969273-kay?shelf=fiction-general" class="actionLinkLite">fiction-general</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer237437527">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10426672761540661166">In a recent New Yorker article Martin Amis wrote “When we say that we love a writer’s work, we are always stretching the truth: what we really mean is that we love about half of it.” I don’t agree with that as a general rule but it sums up my feelings about Anne Tyler pretty well. Some of her books I really love (Dinner at the Homesick Restaurant, Saint Maybe, Back When We Were Grownups) and they’ve become a permanent part of my mental furniture. Others leave me cold (The Accidental Tourist, An</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10426672761540661166">In a recent New Yorker article Martin Amis wrote “When we say that we love a writer’s work, we are always stretching the truth: what we really mean is that we love about half of it.” I don’t agree with that as a general rule but it sums up my feelings about Anne Tyler pretty well. Some of her books I really love (Dinner at the Homesick Restaurant, Saint Maybe, Back When We Were Grownups) and they’ve become a permanent part of my mental furniture. Others leave me cold (The Accidental Tourist, An Amateur Marriage) and I pretty much forget about them as soon as I close the book. Happily, this one falls in the first category. <br /><br />This is Tyler's first book but many of her ongoing themes are already evident here (more so than in A Slipping Down Life, the other NC novel I’ve read). The plot is slight but the characters are engaging, the voices of Shelley and Gram in particular rang true for me. We see them from the outside (like people in real life) so we don’t know these characters intimately but they still come across as real. The six sisters do kind of run together but that seems intentional (and probably true of large families) and “the sisters” definitely have a distinct personality as a whole even if they don’t always as individuals. I like the way that Tyler gives us a slice of these characters lives without revealing all the details of their pasts or concluding too much about their futures. The book left me wanting to know more about their lives both before and after this story. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10426672761540661166">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer33415814">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11223297166262955821">The author has definitely improved as a writer since she wrote this one. This is about Ben Joe and his family. Ben Joe is attending college in NY. He is studying to be a lawyer at Columbia. After learning one of his sister’s has left her husband and moved back home, he feels compelled to go home for a visit right in the middle of a semester. Home is Sandhill, NC. The family of 6 girls and 1 boy (Ben Joe), Mom and Grandma, is quirky at best. Some of the interactions amongst characters in this boo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11223297166262955821">The author has definitely improved as a writer since she wrote this one. This is about Ben Joe and his family. Ben Joe is attending college in NY. He is studying to be a lawyer at Columbia. After learning one of his sister’s has left her husband and moved back home, he feels compelled to go home for a visit right in the middle of a semester. Home is Sandhill, NC. The family of 6 girls and 1 boy (Ben Joe), Mom and Grandma, is quirky at best. Some of the interactions amongst characters in this book are just silly (for a lack of a better word). To me, this wasn’t really a story that had a nice beginning and a happy, or at least concluded end. It was more like a picture in time that ended abruptly. Tyler has definitely developed as a writer, she is one of my favorites. I am glad I had the opportunity to read this book. It just isn’t one of her best. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer212716156">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8917615907438364347">My mother (a babyboomer) introduced me to Tyler's books when I was 15. I've devoured them ever since. I read them before my marriage, while I was married, during my separation, and after my divorce. I've read some of her books 3 &amp; 4 times. Screw those long winded writers of yesteryear that my private liberal arts college told me was brilliant: Tyler takes the cake! She's the woman (in my ridiculous opinion) that John Irving should have married. She would have eaten him alive--so, maybe not.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4426570765838709534">Anne Tyler’s debut novel tracks the self-realization of a young man whose character struggles to negotiate a balance between self-identity and family identity.<br /><br />Tyler's characteristic wit and eccentricity of characters is shown right off the bat even in this first novel.<br /><br />"Seems like you are always loving the people that fly away from you, Ben Joe, and flying away from the people that love you. But if you've decided, this once, to do something the other way, I'll be happy to agree." <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1383564362">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11718339249791129747">E' il primo romanzo della Tyler che leggo e fin da subito la sua scrittura, lineare e molto scorrevole, mi ha catturata e trasportata dentro la storia. Con delicatezza l'autrice ci porta sulla porta di casa Hawkes e ci accompagna con la narrazione all'interno di una famiglia allegra e piena di personaggi, tutti femminili ; infatti Ben Joe, la voce narrante, è cresciuto circondato da donne : la madre e numerose sorelle. L'autrice ci racconta la quotidianità di una famiglia numerosa, squarci di pa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11718339249791129747">E' il primo romanzo della Tyler che leggo e fin da subito la sua scrittura, lineare e molto scorrevole, mi ha catturata e trasportata dentro la storia. Con delicatezza l'autrice ci porta sulla porta di casa Hawkes e ci accompagna con la narrazione all'interno di una famiglia allegra e piena di personaggi, tutti femminili ; infatti Ben Joe, la voce narrante, è cresciuto circondato da donne : la madre e numerose sorelle. L'autrice ci racconta la quotidianità di una famiglia numerosa, squarci di passato che riaffiorano attraverso i ricordi e ci affezioniamo a poco a poco ai personaggi, così ben delineati che ci sembra a volte di vivere le vicende raccontate.Un romanzo leggero e piacevole, che ti riconcilia con le cose semplici della vita e alla fine della lettura ci dispiace un po' lasciare questa casa, che per un po' di tempo è diventata quasi la nostra casa, e chiudere la porta per lasciare i personaggi che abbiamo conosciuto, e amato, tra le pagine del libro.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11718339249791129747">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_60546967">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60546967" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/343797-karen" class="left imgcol" title="Karen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1189093133p2/343797.jpg" alt="Karen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/343797-karen" class="user" title="Karen">Karen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/112321.If_Morning_Ever_Comes" title="Paperback 9780449911785" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer60546967">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16820070368957373988">This is Anne Tyler's first book, and her quirky style is already evident. I enjoyed meeting Ben Joe and his family of six sisters plus his mother and grandmother. Some people are born to write, and while the plot and characters here are not as intricate and multi-faceted as in her later books, we can see that Tyler had found her voice already.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13289563149087413183">I wanted to read her first novel since I have come to respect and enjoy her later works.<br /><br />Anne Tyler was just 22 when she wrote this book and it's worth it just to see her picture, looking somewhat like a long haired Audrey Hepburn, on the dust cover.<br /><br />The book doesn't have much of a plot. It's more like an intense character study of a southern family and the town they inhabit. Ben Joe Hawke wonders about time and place and where he fits in the cosmos. he leaves his law studies in NYC to make sure his 6 sisters, mother and grandma are okay back home in North Carolina. They think they are just fine but he is appalled by his oldest sister's flighty abandonment of her marriage and his <br />mother's refusal to admit that there is anything wrong with it.<br /><br />He also visits the illegitimate child his father sired while he was still married to Ben's mother. For good measure there is an old man dying in town who his grandmother regrets not marrying, and a girl who Ben Joe decides he really loves and needs to bring home with him to New York City.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1504207215">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1504207215" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1473095-holly" class="left imgcol" title="Holly"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Holly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1504207215?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 10, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1473095-holly" class="user" title="Holly">Holly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5054902-if-morning-ever-comes" title="Paperback 9780425061404" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1504207215">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15796729053398944098">Written when Anne Tyler was only twenty-three, "If Morning Ever Comes" is a beautiful book. Reading Anne Tyler is like a long talk with a old friend - one feels good afterwards with a sense of having learned something and of having discovered something new about life. A central theme is the complex relationship been an individual and his or her family.<br /><br />Ben Joe has many sisters. He is off at university at Colombia when he finds out that his oldest sister is back home in Sandhill, that she has left</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15796729053398944098">Written when Anne Tyler was only twenty-three, "If Morning Ever Comes" is a beautiful book. Reading Anne Tyler is like a long talk with a old friend - one feels good afterwards with a sense of having learned something and of having discovered something new about life. A central theme is the complex relationship been an individual and his or her family.<br /><br />Ben Joe has many sisters. He is off at university at Colombia when he finds out that his oldest sister is back home in Sandhill, that she has left her husband and has returned w/ her baby to her childhood home. Feeling some ambivalence towards school and feeling aimless in general, Ben Joe hops a train back home, not sure what he trying to find but sure that something is missing.<br /><br />At the time of this book, Tyler was considered a Southern writer (the big old house, the large family, a strong sense of community, families as female spheres, etc). Her perspective, the single male child in a large family of females, is interesting.<br /><br />Themes:<br />--Marriage as signal of adulthood, taking responsibility, assertion of independence<br />--Returning home as reluctance to leave childhood, as probing wounds of past that shaped who we are today, to see future as a path built by past experiences (Tyler includes the young and old homecoming)<br />--Tension of opposites; Ben Joe's opposite (or is she??) = Joanna; fidelity vs infidelity, young vs old, male vs female, pride vs humility, loneliness vs togetherness<br />--The movement of time and the impact of our decisions on the paths we choose; grandmother didn't marry Mr Dower - how does this single decision change her life?; mortality; the meaning of a life<br />--Memory - how two people remember a life differently<br />--Coming to terms with our lives; Ben Joe realizes that we shape our memories, we work up a script that helps us to come to terms with our past. He finds that he struggles to do this, that he cannot easily state, "Based on this event, I chose this path, which had this impact." In fact, Ben Joe plans to recreate his remembered history w/ Shelley. As the conductor states on the last page, Ben Joe "won't have to change."<br /><br />Critics say this book is flat; I disagree. The characters live simple lives and find simple happiness. The final message might be that we might never fully understand another person, nor ourselves for that matter.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15796729053398944098">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_882166161">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/882166161" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8040729-nereia" class="left imgcol" title="Nereia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1426402618p2/8040729.jpg" alt="Nereia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/882166161?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 24, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8040729-nereia" class="user" title="Nereia">Nereia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/9699816-se-mai-verr-il-mattino" title="Paperback 9788882463960" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8040729-nereia?shelf=women-challenge-2014" class="actionLinkLite">women-challenge-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer882166161">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3695334063024646203"><em>You say the best when you say nothing at all</em><br /><br />Il modo in cui Anne Tyler riesce sempre a dire qualcosa, a trasmettere qualcosa, non raccontando mai nulla di speciale mi stupisce ogni volta che prendo in mano un suo libro.<br /><em>Se mai verrà il mattino</em> è il suo primo romanzo e, nonostante lo stile un po' acerbo, è riuscito ad avvolgermi in un caldo abbraccio così come tutti gli altri suoi romanzi che ho avuto il piacere di divorare. Sì, perché la Tyler ha la capacità di entrarmi dentro e accarezzarmi il cu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3695334063024646203"><em>You say the best when you say nothing at all</em><br /><br />Il modo in cui Anne Tyler riesce sempre a dire qualcosa, a trasmettere qualcosa, non raccontando mai nulla di speciale mi stupisce ogni volta che prendo in mano un suo libro.<br /><em>Se mai verrà il mattino</em> è il suo primo romanzo e, nonostante lo stile un po' acerbo, è riuscito ad avvolgermi in un caldo abbraccio così come tutti gli altri suoi romanzi che ho avuto il piacere di divorare. Sì, perché la Tyler ha la capacità di entrarmi dentro e accarezzarmi il cuore come pochi altri scrittori riescono a fare. Con me e il mio grinzoso cuoricino, almeno.<br />Protagonista di questo romanzo, come sempre nei romanzi della Tyler del resto, è una famiglia rumorosa e sconclusionata.<br />E io nei romanzi che raccontano le vicende, gli amori e i dispiaceri delle famiglie sconclusionate ci sguazzo allegramente dentro. Proprio come i bambini che si divertono saltellando appositamente dentro le pozzanghere, io saltello appositamente dentro i romanzi di questo tipo.<br />Le famiglie mi incuriosiscono, mi hanno sempre affascianata. Forse perché un po' soffro del non aver mai avuto una famiglia numerosa e chiassosa come quelle dei romanzi. Le ho sempre vissute indirettamente quelle come la famiglia Hawkes e ho sempre provato un po' di invidia, lo ammetto, per quegli amici che avevano la fortuna di essere circondati di zii pazzi, cugini indisciplinati e nonne simpatiche. O forse perché sono un tipo romantico e mi piace pensare alla famiglia come una sorta di branco, dove ci si aiuta l'un l'altra e ci si accetta così, squilibrati mentalmente per quanto si è. Qualunque sia il motivo di fondo, già dalle prime righe di questo romanzo, sapevo che non sarei rimasta per niente delusa.<br />Con dolcezza, Anne Tyler ci accompagna sulla porta di casa Hawkes e ci lascia lì, sul portico accanto al dondolo, aspettando che qualcuno venga ad aprirci. È Ben Joe, un ragazzo ancora troppo giovane e insicuro, che ci accoglie e ci invita a varcare la soglia. Da quel momento le nostre giornate non saranno più le stesse.<br />Adesso che ne ho terminato la lettura è come se fossi ancora lì, in compagnia delle innumerevoli donne Hawkes. Mi sembra di sentire i loro passi frettolosi sulla moquette, di vedere le liste della spesa attaccate al frigorifero, di osservarle mentre guardano la tv in vestaglia.<br />È questo che fa Anne Tyler, è questo che fa a me. Mi fa affezionare alle famiglie di cui mi racconta. Non ho usato il pronome personale sbagliato, ho scritto che "mi" racconta perché è proprio quello che intendo. Perché, in ogni suo libro, sembra sempre che lei si rivolga proprio a noi e non al lettore come entità. Manca solo che ci chiami per nome prima di iniziare a raccontarci una storia.<br />Ho avuto l'impressione – e non solo durante la lettura di questo romanzo – che lei fosse seduta accanto a me, magari attorno al tavolo della sua cucina con una tazza di tè fumante tra le mani, e mi dicesse qualcosa di simile a: "Nereia, oggi voglio raccontarti la storia di un mio amico, Ben Joe, e della sua straordinaria famiglia".<br />Nulla di particolarmente importante sconvolge la vita di Ben Joe e di tutte le donne Hawkes, non nella parte della loro vita che Anne Tyler decide di mostrarci, perlomeno. Le cose veramente significative che hanno segnato la vita di ognuno di loro sono già accadute da diverso tempo quando la narrazione ha inizio. Fanno, così, parte di ricordi ormai lontani e quasi sfocati che, però, rivestono comunque un ruolo abbastanza importante all'interno della storia. Non manca occasione per far ricordare a Ben Joe il padre ormai defunto, una vacanza avvenuta anni luce or sono, un vestito indossato da una delle sue sorelle quando andava ancora al liceo. Il tutto senza che sembri messo lì per muovere a compassione il lettore o per riempire dei vuoti all'interno della trama. I ricordi ci sono perché sono parte della storia, dei personaggi. Se Ben Joe non aprisse una finestrella sul suo passato e non ci permettesse di affacciarci a sbirciare, questo libro non avrebbe motivo di esistere. Strano a dirsi, ma non poi così strano se si parla della Tyler. Inutile che mi impegni, non riesco a spiegarmi meglio di così. Ad Anne Tyler riesce bene tutto, anche scrivere un romanzo che racconta una settimana soltanto e una vita intera, contemporaneamente. <br /><br />Recensione tratta dal mio blog: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://librangoloacuto.blogspot.it/2014/03/recensione-se-mai-verra-il-mattino.html">Se mai verrà il mattino</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3695334063024646203">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16626163992139275303">This is the first book that I have read by Anne Tyler: I picked it up on a whim having never heard of her because I came across many of her novels at a book sale and reviews of her work seemed good. I was not terribly impressed by this one, but after finding out this was her first novel, and she wrote it at 22 I may give her another whirl.<br /><br />Ben Joe is the only son in a house filled with women: mom, sisters, and grandmother. When he finds out that his oldest sister has left her husband to come back</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16626163992139275303">This is the first book that I have read by Anne Tyler: I picked it up on a whim having never heard of her because I came across many of her novels at a book sale and reviews of her work seemed good. I was not terribly impressed by this one, but after finding out this was her first novel, and she wrote it at 22 I may give her another whirl.<br /><br />Ben Joe is the only son in a house filled with women: mom, sisters, and grandmother. When he finds out that his oldest sister has left her husband to come back home, he takes a break from college and heads home to check on the family. He is the man of the house, ever since his father died, but seems to have never had a firm grasp on his role, or who he is. To borrow a turn of phrase from the fantastic film "Steel Magnolias," Ben Joe "doesn't know whether to scratch his watch or wind his book.<br /><br />I would say that this book was almost interesting, but fairly underwhelming. There were some good elements, but I didn't care for the end. Overall an easy and pleasant enough read, and a great first effort for her age, but not one I'll keep for the home library.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13763579659890853123">I would rate this a 3.5 if I could. I have always enjoyed Anne Tyler's books and she is one of my "go to" authors when I'm undecided what to read. I grabbed this book to take on vacation. I enjoyed it, but it was not as captivating as some of the others I have read and was not set in Baltimore, like most of hers are.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText13763579659890853123">I would rate this a 3.5 if I could. I have always enjoyed Anne Tyler's books and she is one of my "go to" authors when I'm undecided what to read. I grabbed this book to take on vacation. I enjoyed it, but it was not as captivating as some of the others I have read and was not set in Baltimore, like most of hers are. It was filled with interesting, eclectic characters and situations but just didn't seem as well developed. However, when I read the author interview at the end of the book I discovered that it was one of her first books. In that aspect, I was glad I did read it and can appreciate how much she has matured as an author over the years. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer907672407">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5020664206040943983">This book didn't quite make me want to hang myself with my own hair, but it came close. It was sort of an unsettling, vaguely depressing short story (are there any others?) writ large; I felt at times like I did when I was 15 years old and it was a rainy winter Saturday afternoon at MaMaw and PaPaw's house in Garden City and I was "trapped" there by lack of a driver's license and the thought that that in fact might be how I would have to spend the rest of my entire life. Who knows, though? That</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5020664206040943983">This book didn't quite make me want to hang myself with my own hair, but it came close. It was sort of an unsettling, vaguely depressing short story (are there any others?) writ large; I felt at times like I did when I was 15 years old and it was a rainy winter Saturday afternoon at MaMaw and PaPaw's house in Garden City and I was "trapped" there by lack of a driver's license and the thought that that in fact might be how I would have to spend the rest of my entire life. Who knows, though? That might've been Ms. Tyler's intention, to evoke exactly such an emotional reaction from her reader. It was written well.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1265879630">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6187172016123305782">In Buenos Aires this past January, on sabbatical, I decided to re-read If Morning Ever Comes, Anne Tyler’s first book, which I’d read before on a sabbatical in 1992 in Madrid. I liked the idea of re-visiting my own life. And I love all of Anne Tyler. I can never guess where she’s taking me in a book, which is the highest praise I can pay to any author. When I get to the end of a Tyler novel, I often have to sit and think about where she’s left me. Both cases proved true even in re-reading If Mor</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6187172016123305782">In Buenos Aires this past January, on sabbatical, I decided to re-read If Morning Ever Comes, Anne Tyler’s first book, which I’d read before on a sabbatical in 1992 in Madrid. I liked the idea of re-visiting my own life. And I love all of Anne Tyler. I can never guess where she’s taking me in a book, which is the highest praise I can pay to any author. When I get to the end of a Tyler novel, I often have to sit and think about where she’s left me. Both cases proved true even in re-reading If Morning Ever Comes. Over the years I’d forgotten more than a sense of the book. I couldn’t remember whether the protagonist was a man or a woman, although I recalled that the book began with the protagonist taking an overnight train from New York home to a small North Carolina town for an unplanned visit. I found that, in fact, protagonist Ben Joe is playing hooky from law school to check on his home full of sisters and mother and grandmother, perhaps to see if any of them had noticed--really noticed--that he was gone. On long nocturnal walks about town he rekindles his relationship with his girlfriend from high school years.<br />I love the ambiguity of Ben Joe, an ambiguity that makes him, like many later Tyler protagonists, unsure of himself and of people and happenings around him. In my opinion Tyler, with this first novel published at 23, found her voice. <br />I decided to work re-reading Anne Tyler into all of the other books I read or, in the case of a number of books, start and don’t read. By now I’ve re-read The Tin-Can Tree, A Slipping-Down Life, The Clock Winder, Celestial Navigation, Searching for Caleb, and Earthly Possessions. I’ve savored each, like drinking a glass of fine wine or the once-a-week manhattan allowed me by my cardiologist. Tyler has confirmed her place as one of my all-time favorite authors.<br />(Note: I five-star all books to opt out of ranking any relative to all others I’ve liked in my 67 years, a chore that would keep me awake nights. “If I give five stars to The Taxi that Hurried, my favorite when I was five, then…”)<br /></span>

          </span>

        rated it

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Summer Cottage Readers</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11964994-anthony?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11964994-anthony?shelf=ebooks" class="actionLinkLite">ebooks</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11964994-anthony?shelf=large-print" class="actionLinkLite">large-print</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer397483702">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12872486651277434137">It was a dear friend of mine that introduced me to this author. He's actually a big fan of Anne Tyler. And after reading another novel, this one, and others in waiting, I can completely understand why. They are a pleasure to read.<br /><br />Being introduced to Ben Joe Hawkes, I have to say, I've never come across a main character like this one before. He's a worrier, socially awkward, overbearing, but never seems to have the courage to truly say exactly what's on his mind. Unmotivated, discouraged, introve</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12872486651277434137">It was a dear friend of mine that introduced me to this author. He's actually a big fan of Anne Tyler. And after reading another novel, this one, and others in waiting, I can completely understand why. They are a pleasure to read.<br /><br />Being introduced to Ben Joe Hawkes, I have to say, I've never come across a main character like this one before. He's a worrier, socially awkward, overbearing, but never seems to have the courage to truly say exactly what's on his mind. Unmotivated, discouraged, introverted. And when he does finally say something, it comes out all wrong. A complete outsider always looking in, either asking too many questions or internally over analyzing. He loves his family passionately, but doesn't and can't accept that life goes on without him. I don't think I could truly find one word that describes Ben Joe. Am I giving away too much?<br /><br />Throughout the novel I laughed, shook my head in disbelief, got frustrated, and wanting to reach in and shake the main character's shoulders and yell out, "Are you kidding me?!", right to his face. Anne Tyler is a brilliant creator of simple folk. Nothing really was over exaggerated. He's the only brother, the second eldest, of many sisters. All of Ben Joe's sisters treat him "kindness" and simply humor him no matter what he says. His widowed mother does her best with pride. His grandmother from his father's side is just a delight (half-sarcasm). And his father... well, I'll give away too much to try and explain the father. You see, there's one thing that you -- the reader -- will know about Ben Joe throughout the novel: he doesn't like change. Why? You'll just have to read the entire story to understand why.<br /><br />Without giving it away, the ending left me shaking my head with unanswered questions that I had mentally asked myself in regards to Ben Joe. I wanted just a little more than what I was given. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12872486651277434137">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6966977346622976062">I've read quite a few novels by Anne Tyler. This is her first, written when she was 22. Although nothing much happens in this book, it kept me interested all the way through. She always puts quirky characters in her books, and in this one it's Ben Joe's gran.<br /><br />Ben Joe leaves Law School in NYC to travel home to Sandhill, NC because he hears that his sister has left her husband and returned home.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText6966977346622976062">I've read quite a few novels by Anne Tyler. This is her first, written when she was 22. Although nothing much happens in this book, it kept me interested all the way through. She always puts quirky characters in her books, and in this one it's Ben Joe's gran.<br /><br />Ben Joe leaves Law School in NYC to travel home to Sandhill, NC because he hears that his sister has left her husband and returned home. He lives in a family with 6 sisters, his mother and his dead father's mother. He seems to not be a part of their life, they buzz around him and he is confused by the noise and action. He visits his father's mistress and an old girlfriend, and after about a week returns to NY, this time with his girlfriend in tow, as they are going to get married. He doesn't seem to love her much, but feels that she needs him. He imagines his future, with a wife and a son that he doesn't understand, but that doesn't bother him.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_764565255">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/764565255?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 15, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3582853-karen-michele" class="user" title="Karen Michele">Karen Michele</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2128723.If_Morning_Ever_Comes" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780804108843" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3582853-karen-michele?shelf=14-rws-winter" class="actionLinkLite">14-rws-winter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer764565255">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5800405783907338819">I enjoy going back and reading an author's debut book and getting to know how that author has matured since starting out on his or her career. Anne Tyler's first book, If Morning Ever Comes, is a journey into that history and also a journey into a time period from my past and I enjoyed the experience of revisiting 1964. I was about ten years younger than the main character, Ben Joe, but I still remember the time without cell phones and the ability to take off around town and be on your own disco</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5800405783907338819">I enjoy going back and reading an author's debut book and getting to know how that author has matured since starting out on his or her career. Anne Tyler's first book, If Morning Ever Comes, is a journey into that history and also a journey into a time period from my past and I enjoyed the experience of revisiting 1964. I was about ten years younger than the main character, Ben Joe, but I still remember the time without cell phones and the ability to take off around town and be on your own disconnected from your family and the stresses of the world for awhile. The book is more character then plot driven and I enjoyed getting inside Ben Joe's head. The story picked up when grandma became more important in the book and the best writing is in the descriptions and dialog in scenes including her near the end of the book. I haven't read Anne Tyler in a while and I will be remedying that situation soon!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5800405783907338819">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/112321.If_Morning_Ever_Comes" title="Paperback 9780449911785" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1238612164">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13590382602021895361">This is one of Anne Tyler's first books. I tend to like books with a clear plot and steer away from character development fiction. Although the plot was secondary in this novel I did enjoy the character of Ben Joe and his thoughts and drifting ways. I will read more of Anne Tyler's writing, but will have to space it out with something more gripping. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer524434051">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4180870923957824748">Ben Joe Hawkes suddenly leaves his law studies in New York and takes the train home to North Carolina to check up on his family, which consists of his mother, grandmother and 6 sisters. Probably taking place in the late 50's or 60's, as the only male Ben Joe is considered the head of the family. A combination of his dislike of law school and New York, homesickness, and his feeling that he's not getting all the news about his family's activities prompts the sudden visit. There's not much action i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4180870923957824748">Ben Joe Hawkes suddenly leaves his law studies in New York and takes the train home to North Carolina to check up on his family, which consists of his mother, grandmother and 6 sisters. Probably taking place in the late 50's or 60's, as the only male Ben Joe is considered the head of the family. A combination of his dislike of law school and New York, homesickness, and his feeling that he's not getting all the news about his family's activities prompts the sudden visit. There's not much action in the story, but we get to know more about him, his family and a few other townspeople.<br /><br />I loved the style of writing in this book, which was Anne Tyler's first published novel. Although there didn't seem to be any particular point to the book, the words and dialogue helped me visualize very clear and interesting characters in my mind.</span>

When Claire Bennett\'s hus&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText17644635711425095776\" style=\"display:none\"&gt; From Joan Medlicott, the nationally bestselling creator of the beloved Ladies of Covington series, comes an inspiring, hope-filled tale of a woman who finds the courage to begin a journey that will lead to a whole new life.  When Claire Bennett\'s husband died, she felt directionless. Their thriving antiques business and beautiful house in the Hamptons, the social scene and her volunteer work -- all seemed empty without Phillip. Estranged from her adult daughter and son, Claire knows that in the depths of her heart she still mourns a terrible loss from a tragic accident years ago.  Fleeing her memories, Claire moves to a condo in Florida, then impulsively leaves to visit her engaged daughter in North Carolina. From the sandy beaches of Boca Raton to a tiny farm tucked high in the Blue Ridge Mountains, Claire gains self-awareness through the unexpected kindness of strangers, and finally forces herself to confront some hard truths from the past.  Finding a joy in life that has been missing for many years, Claire at last reaches out to her son and daughter. And when the healing of old wounds leads her to a new love, Claire realizes that her travels have brought her to a place where she will never again walk alone.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/457.Anne_Tyler">About Anne Tyler</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/457.Anne_Tyler"><img alt="457" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1332881249p2/457.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1532310303775861301"><strong>Anne Tyler</strong> was born in Minneapolis, Minnesota, in 1941 and grew up in Raleigh, North Carolina. She graduated at nineteen from Duke University and went on to do graduate work in Russian studies at Columbia University. <em> <a title="The Beginner's Goodbye by Anne Tyler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12482658.The_Beginner_s_Goodbye">The Beginner's Goodbye</a> </em> is Anne Tyler's nineteenth novel; her eleventh, <em> <a title="Breathing Lessons by Anne Tyler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons">Breathing Lessons</a> </em>, was awarded the Pulitzer Prize in 1988. She is a member of the American Academy of Arts a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1532310303775861301"><strong>Anne Tyler</strong> was born in Minneapolis, Minnesota, in 1941 and grew up in Raleigh, North Carolina. She graduated at nineteen from Duke University and went on to do graduate work in Russian studies at Columbia University. <em>
  <a title="The Beginner's Goodbye by Anne Tyler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12482658.The_Beginner_s_Goodbye">The Beginner's Goodbye</a>
</em> is Anne Tyler's nineteenth novel; her eleventh, <em>
  <a title="Breathing Lessons by Anne Tyler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons">Breathing Lessons</a>
</em>, was awarded the Pulitzer Prize in 1988. She is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters.</span>
